Free Talk

The Rise of Literary Contingency (Tokyo Correspondence) 213

— Hongying

Recently, in the Japanese literary world, there has been a widespread debate on "contingency." The reason for this debate is due to two main facts: first, the issue of the so-called "purity" or "popularity" of literature, that is, to make literature not lose its "purity" as literature, not fall into the path of boring "popular literature," but also be rich in popular interest; second, the issue of romanticism, that is, in view of the mechanical and dull dryness of realism, the active expression is required. (This has been supported by some people led by Kataoka Teppei, forming the "Social Romantic School.") These two issues have a common point, that is, they both want to "make it interesting." When discussing this "interestingization," the focus of the problem shifted to "contingency."

Almost every active critic and writer has been drawn into the vortex of this "contingency theory" debate. Although the object of the problem is in literature, the scope involved includes philosophy, physics, statistics, and so on. Although the opinions of each person in the debate vary, they can be summarized into two major categories in essence, and each major category can be further divided into smaller categories.

The first category is represented by the views of Yokomitsu Riichi, Nakagami Yoichi, Ishiwara Jun, and Kataoka Teppei. The second category is represented by Moriyama Kei, Ogiwara Naka, and some of Tosaka Jun's views, which inherit the theoretical system of Kurahara Korehito and Kawaguchi Hiroshi.

Yokomitsu Riichi believes that the current Japanese popular literature has two elements: one is appealing to sentimentality, and the other is utilizing contingency. He advocates that pure popular literature in the future should abandon the former element—sentimentality, and adopt the latter—contingency. He said: "The contingency (temporality or specificity) in pure novels, or the deformed part of the special movement that naturally occurs due to the concentration of the daily life (necessity or universality) that constitutes most of that novel: or it intensifies the previous daily life, making that contingency possible to occur, making that contingency occur. If contingency appears in the work without one of these two, then the contingency expressed will definitely become sentimental." Yokomitsu Riichi is a so-called liberal literary person, so his views are quite sharp. He thoroughly explained a part of the essential relationship between contingency and necessity here. However, he only believes that contingency is the concentration of necessity, and he does not know that necessity is the concentration of contingency. He recognizes necessity as a kind of daily life and denies that necessity can become another possibility of higher expression.

Nakagami Yoichi's theory of contingency is concretely advocated in his "Theory of Contingent Literature" in the June issue of "Shincho." Although this thing is only a few short pages, it has cited fourteen or five famous scholars from physics, philosophy, and literature, and he has fallen into the quagmire of formal logic. Ishiwara Jun's theory of contingency has a more systematic opinion. He starts from the "epistemology of new quantum mechanics" and its statistical method, all the way to "statistical thinking" (i.e., statistical phenomena in physics and social sciences), and thus establishes his theory of contingency.

"New quantum mechanics" believes that electrons or light are particles and waves at the same time, and it is impossible to accurately determine their position and speed at the same time. Electrons disrupt the original causality of the system being measured, and it is also impossible to measure the position and speed in the purely pure system; therefore, it is impossible to infer the future by the law of causality. Here, "new quantum mechanics" produced the negation of the law of causality. Ishiwara Jun treats the law of causality as necessity, and therefore believes that what cannot be known by this law of causality is contingency. This is the "agnosticism of new quantum mechanics." He also said that thinkers of statistics believe that there is "probability" in the accumulation of this contingency, and they want to drive the concepts of causality and necessity out of the world of learning. Learning is following the "world of probability," and "the world of contingency that cannot be fully covered by this has long belonged outside the scope of science," "We should take this as the theme of literature." Ishiwara Jun has here set up a boundary line of epistemology that cannot be crossed between learning and art, advocating literature with psychology as the theme that cannot be pursued by the law of causality. However, this kind of literature is just "literature of madhouses, confused and crowded futurist literature, and a sentimental rhapsody mixed singing." Ishiwara Jun's claim represents the social consciousness of the few people in modern times who are afraid of the necessity of history.

Kataoka Teppei's theory of contingency is a kind of common sense theory of contingency. The meaning of his contingency is to express "unexpected" and "unpredictable" thoughts. He cited an example: one day he met an old friend - a beautiful woman - in a car, "The novel started from here. If there is this contingency, then any other daily life will have no meaning." This kind of contingency in common sense is completely the existence of subjective concepts, not objective reality.

Next, let's talk about the views of the second category. In 1931, when the international community did not have a clear idea of the issue of contingency, Kurahara Korehito correctly said, "What is not essential to an individual system (or process) is the contingency of that process." For example, the European War was caused by a young Serbian man assassinating the Austrian crown prince. This event was a contingency for the imperialist war. Even without this contingency, the war would have broken out through another contingency.

Kawaguchi Hiroshi further accepted this achievement and said: "Necessary things and contingent things combine to express the surface of phenomena." Necessity is discovered through contingency, and contingency is transformed into necessity.

Moriyama Kei further developed this theory. He pointed out the meaning, duties, and functions of contingency. He pointed out the objectivity of contingency and its role in accelerating or delaying history. Tosaka Jun, Ogiwara Naka, etc. believe that the so-called theory of contingency this time is a "problem of possibility and reality," "the necessary category of realism and even romanticism is not contingency, but the possibility of reality and the freedom of reality." This is quite concise.

Squeezing 214

— Hu Yifan

The days fly by quickly, and it's almost been two months since I last wrote three articles.

"This is terrible! Time wasted and no results achieved, not to mention I still have to make a living!"

I鞭策 myself in this way three or four times.

I summoned unparalleled courage, sat down at my writing desk, ordered myself to grip the pen holder between my fingers, and shouted from the depths of my heart:

"Write! Write hard! Why aren't you writing?"

I sat blankly at my writing desk with a pen in my hand, time slipping away minute by minute, the manuscript paper on the desk still a blank page. My gloomy brain, as if coated with lime, had blocked every tiny pore.

Turning it over and over, I still couldn't write a single word.

"Heavy and dull! Useless brain!"

All I could do was curse myself again.

The environment now is as calm as can be: the room has never been as peaceful as it is this morning. The children are making not a sound, and my mother is fast asleep in bed, snoring away. Outside, the sounds of even the peddlers are gone. The only commotion is the murmuring of frogs outside the fence, and the birds singing in the short branches of the shrubs in the neighbor's garden; they are here to调剂 this stifling air, could they possibly trigger my literary thoughts! Then, why can't I write?

I took a deep breath, put down my pen, stuck a cigarette between my fingers, and tidied my scattered hair a little. Secretly, I still wanted to鼓舞 my灵思.

"Novel, essay, miscellaneous thoughts, what should I write!"

My thoughts are not organized at all, and I don't know where to start. I switched the cigarette back and forth between my hands, moving up and down around the desk. I lowered my head and stretched, I picked up the pen, and then put it down.

One cigarette was burned, and I quickly lit another. When I really couldn't write a word, I simply played with the smoke rings. Strangely enough, I couldn't even make smoke rings today. Angrily, I slammed the half-smoked cigarette into the spittoon with a *thud*.

I immediately lit another one.

But there was still not a single word on the manuscript paper!

Inspiration is truly not coming today!

I stared blankly at the blank manuscript paper? I frowned, *smack*, and I slammed down the pen again.

"Why do I have to write this damn thing? Can't I do something else? Cursed soulless writing career"

When I hated it, I made up my mind to give up in despair.

"Might as well throw out all that damn stuff on the bookshelf."

But in the blink of an eye, I saw the innocent smiling faces of the children on the small couch beside me, and my mother, leaning up, her eyes revealing dark circles from staying up late writing last night, brought on by excessive fatigue, and I felt a bit of stimulation again.

"I can't be so romantic! Why can't I write?"

I immediately corrected myself and summoned my courage again.

*Tss*, I threw away the half-smoked cigarette again and picked up the pen again.

But what to write? Novel? Essay? Or miscellaneous thoughts? I haven't even thought of a title today! As soon as I touched on this, I became even more disturbed.

I smoked another cigarette, put down the pen, my brain felt as if it were heavily stuffed with lime, not a bit of air通气.

I slowly blurred my past experiences, which, although not rich, were not entirely impoverished, and even wanted to forget them all.

Reality, I am so far away from it.

What to write? I really feel a little sad for myself. A corroded life!

Love (5) 215

— By S. Yersegev-Yinski, translated by Su Ming

He passed the first week not badly. He used his axe all day long, making firewood while the snow wasn't too deep, to prepare for Changchun's winter. He also smoked some fish, in case the weather was too cold to venture out. He made a shovel to clear the snow from the ice on the river. His axe became his best friend, along with his net and rifle. The fire burned brightly in the cave, and he was so happy that he began to think of the school teacher Yarosha, and sometimes even said aloud: "In a room like this, two people could live well." But he always had to add, "If she didn't have a red head and a black heart."

One morning, when he opened the door (when there was a large amount of積物, the door always opened inward, not outward), he jumped up in alarm. Right in front of the door, hidden under the pine tree, crouched a huge wolf,　 ready to pounce on his throat. Savaka barely managed to slam the door shut. He grabbed his gun. When he opened the door again, *whack*, the wolf was still standing there, a mother wolf, the leader of a pack. He killed her with his first shot, but below, under the pine tree, stood the whole pack of wolves howling. Some of them were retreating to the riverbank, and Savaka noticed that he was surrounded by a large pack of wolves in the forest that night.

He brought the dead wolf's pelt into the cave, but now he only dared go out to catch fish with his rifle. He knew that once wolves discovered a person in the forest, they would never give up. Two days later, in reality, they followed him to the river, and there were no fewer than a dozen of them. Savaka fired twice before they ran away. His cave now had two more wolf pelts. He threw the carcasses on the snow. On the first night, they were吞　 by the rest of the wolf pack, just like the one he had killed before.

Thus began a hunt that lasted a whole winter—a two-sided hunt, the wolves hunting Savaka, and Savaka hunting them. In the winter, he got a total of nine wolf pelts. But he no longer went too far from the cave, and his skis lay unused in the corner. Occasionally, if he was lucky, he would catch a 　鴣 near the cave, and then he could stop catching fish for a while.

Then the days began to be without daylight, only dim. There was no sound in the cave except for the howling of wolves, the occasional啼呌 of big cats, and the roar of frequent blizzards. Savaka carried a notebook with him and wanted to write something. But he wrote so badly, almost like drawing, that he used all the clean paper for cigarettes. Besides, there was really nothing to write about. A cave is finally a cave, winter is like all winters, wolves are just wolves, the forest is just a forest, and the river is no different from other rivers—what else is there to write about?

On the Yangtze Steamer (3) 216

— Ye Zi

The mother compassionately wrapped the child and brought it to the产妇's side, covering her with a blanket and saying:

"We're almost to Jiujiang, take good care of this child... Congratulations! It's a beautiful little girl!... We'll go and try to think of a solution for you..."

"What! Your child?...”

The tea servers ran over again, this time on the order of the purser, to drive her ashore. The two of them dragged her away without saying a word, one of them rolled up the blanket full of blood 汚 that we gave her.

The boat stopped.

The mother's entire charitable cause had completely failed. When she watched the tea servers drag the产妇 ashore while picking up the scattered copper coins and 洋钱 on the ground, she almost cried. (End)

Correspondence 218

— Ding

If it is necessary and possible, then please unfold and read the diary and many letters that I left you in the past. I think: This will be beneficial to you.

Although various scars are engraved on my body, they are indeed the only marks that motivate me and encourage me to struggle. In short, my ideal, my deeds, and that kind of natural and innocent affection for you, you, who have been my sincere friend for many years, should understand.

But, the gap between us is like a deep chasm.

Why did we have such terrible things happen this time?

Regarding this answer, I feel unfortunate.

Thinking about the interruption of our six or seven years of long-standing friendship, because of me, I heard a friend praise you: you therefore feel that life is boring, and you suddenly feel disheartened about people and affairs. Why did you think of such a cowardly place? Do you think that dying—dying in vain like this—will arouse people's sympathy for you? Will this end your困窘 fate? Can this get rid of this evil and卑汚 world?

No. That way of thinking is wrong. The sins of the world will not decrease because of your death. Darkness still envelops our surroundings. Pain still closely follows you.

Don't be so痴吧, they will treat you with a mocking attitude. And you are just in vain, meaningless, worthless like a dog, being躱 in a hole, are you willing? Are you willing to sacrifice your own precious life?

This is not worth it. And, that's such a stupid thing!

Whenever I am touched by these things, intense and tragic pain is stirred up in my heart. Thinking of the warm taste of your care for me, arising from your sincere love for me, I, who have been your faithful, intimate, and helpful friend, should shoulder what a great responsibility for your future.

Struggle, seek survival from the bloodbath!

Don't make a single gamble with your own life.

Although the earth is filled with the groans of endless suffering,

But in it, you will hear pleasant sounds,

That is the symphony of great life, and happiness is entrusted in it!

Random Thoughts

Foreigners Forbid Overseas Chinese from Reading Chinese Books and Newspapers 219

— Xing An

In recent years, our overseas Chinese compatriots have also suffered national disasters along with the motherland, and have been bullied by foreigners everywhere. Those who have been ordered to be expelled have returned to the motherland in batches like stray dogs. Those who still live abroad are constantly subjected to unreasonable oppression. This time, the Chinese and natives in the Dutch East Indies had armed clashes, and the lives and properties of overseas Chinese compatriots are even more in danger. But the suffering of our overseas Chinese compatriots is not only economically squeezed out, but even the freedom to read books and newspapers is interfered with. Previously, the Siamese government's implementation of banning Chinese schools, forcing Chinese schools to teach Siamese, and prohibiting the import of Chinese newspapers and magazines can be described as the ultimate in oppression. Singapore authorities have recently taken steps to ban the use of Chinese textbooks in overseas Chinese schools. Most recently, the government of Dutch West Borneo has gone even further, and even wants to burn Chinese books on a regular basis. All of these retrograde actions not only hinder the education of overseas Chinese, but also insult the dignity of China. It is the due right of overseas Chinese to read Chinese books and newspapers. Foreigners must interfere arbitrarily, which is to deprive people of their freedom.

Checking the foreigners' restrictions on our overseas Chinese compatriots from reading Chinese books and newspapers, their malicious intentions are deeply worth noting. For example, this time the government of Dutch West Borneo implemented a ban on Chinese textbooks, because it was discovered that some of the student compositions revised by the teacher of the Kundian Good Shepherd School were considered "uninspected", "the wording was激烈的", "containing political incitement", and "malice to alienate the nation", so the authorities believed that it violated local laws and decided to burn it. This kind of action is a bit too unreasonable. It is heard that the Overseas Chinese Federation was extremely indignant after receiving the report and will make some representation. But how should we express it? There must be a practical way to resist.

Pearl River Night Moon 220

— Ni

Looking at the full, round, crystal-clear, and bright moon in the mid-sky, blowing the习习 light and quick breeze, the beautiful scenery of the Pearl River Night Moon suddenly floats into my mind. Indeed, it once intoxicated my childish heart and spent a part of my very valuable youth! How can I not miss it, eternally miss it? Although I have shouldered the heavy burden of a tedious home, walking with heavy steps, and moving towards the ethereal and bitter taste of the journey of life, I have left the beautiful Pearl River scenery that once intoxicated my childish heart for a long time. However, its tranquil beauty, the wide and winding river surface, the smooth like a large mirror, the light,碧绿 clear waves, the "spring colors" inside the boat buildings and painted boats, and the lush, verdant, and飘逸荔枝 orchards on both sides of the river... all these beautiful postures are deeply imprinted on my 残伤 heart, and whenever the jade plate-like moon hangs in the deep blue sky, my 잔상 broken heart seems to be刮 up a狂大 wind,掀起了 countless ripples of waves, recalling the past joy, and the present潦倒, 凄凉, the Pearl River 풍월's relics, old feelings, are all勾撩起来 by the coy and crystal-clear moon's smile.

In this blazing heat of the scorching heat, people, like snakes in the tropics, are tired, and the people of 棉市 (Guangzhou) will definitely feel the terribleness of the 溽暑 and be forced to come to the Pearl River. Therefore, the swimming grounds in the eastern and western suburbs will also begin to feel not cold and clear, lonely, and鬧哄哄翻騰着 many健美哥儿們 and娘儿們. Whenever dusk approached, the sun收斂了 its hot and poisonous light, quietly and lazily钻沈 into the back of the lychee orchards on the west bank of the river, then, this wide and winding stream of the Pearl River, the west suburb of the branch of the Lychee Bay, in the gentle飄拂 of the cool evening wind, it feels particularly縹緻,秀美, and full of a 로맨틱 atmosphere. At that time, in my innocent and innocent heart, I really didn't know that there was a so-called辛, 酸, 苦, 澀 taste in the world, my whole mind and body were 심취 in the beautiful scenery like a美人儿's embrace. On the nights when the moon was round and round, the quiet and tranquil Pearl River's澄碧 flowing water was dotted with countless twinkling and brilliant皎潔银光, at this time, I always liked to偕着 a few知友, rent a quick little boat 欵乃乃, 动荡 to the middle of the river, sitting in the cabin, 미폐着 my eyes, quietly listening to the slight and rhythmic sound of the flowing water激荡 from under the boat, or the low回清脆小調 song of the boat girl抱在懷里 on the楼头 of the painted boats on both sides of the bank, this is also a别有风趣赏心乐事的玩意儿! If the wine comes, you may wish to沽 a few pounds of "Qingmei", and buy some seasonal water vegetables, while singing to the wine, while appreciating the晶莹皎洁 Pearl River Night Moon in the mid-sky, letting the boat float down with the flowing water, and when the wine意闌珊 reaches the飄飄然境地, it is okay to引吭 high song,大開喉嚨, to come to a没有调儿吟哦 "浓" sing it, if the throat is hoarse or thirsty, you can also 捨舟登陸, in the garden-style swimming room on the embankment, casually have a cup of shaved ice,潤潤嗓音: If you feel a little hungry in your stomach, and you are lazy to go to Xiguan for refreshments, there is the famous "艇仔粥" in the river, which you can任凭 you eat a淋漓痛快. When I recall the beautiful "Pearl River Night Moon", there is a bit of酸溜溜 in my heart. Ah, I have迈进 the boundless journey of life.

Returning Home - A True Chapter 221

— Ai Tu

From the North Shanghai Railway Station, I boarded a third-class carriage, the train carrying me southward as if in a frenzy. It was morning, and the sun, with the tenderness and shyness of a virgin, was peeking out with a reddish glow from between the bamboo groves of the east or the valleys of the high mountains. It was beautiful and lovely, and it contained a deep, rustic country air. It was also like an innocent child, smiling with its mouth open.

The train roared with a frenzied tune. The sound of the iron wheels grinding against the snake-like rails was so harsh it nearly deafened the travelers.

From the train window, one could see a vast expanse of emerald green fields, with soft grass swaying in the breeze. On the high mountains, apart from the colors peeking through the dense forests, there were sparsely scattered tombs hiding the skulls of the dead, silently squatting among the peaks. We can see these relics everywhere, and we can see the southern people's reverence and filial piety towards their ancestors. However, I could only glance at these scenes with a faint eye from inside the train, feeling nothing in particular.

Only the thoughts of a wanderer missing his home were especially encouraging.

At this moment, I thought of my old, dilapidated home. The old home stood desolate in that declining village, and my poor mother was waiting with wide eyes for her son, who had been wandering far away for many years, to return. Yes, I will never forget that I left her a long time ago in a moment of confusion, quietly escaping from that terrible circle.

However, what am I going back for now? Can

Page 20

that pitiful home still offer me any reason to linger? No! No! I hate the dark hometown, I've hated it since I was a child. Yet, I love my poor old mother. Isn't her hair white and aren't there many wrinkles on her brow? Doesn't she love her young son?

Thinking this, my heart unconsciously became tense and sad.

Quickly, the high mountains and green waters flashed past my eyes, one after another.

When the train arrived at a station in my hometown, the sun was radiating a vivid virgin-like color, gently welcoming the returning wanderer. Getting off the train, the station was still the same as many years ago, except that two new Western-style houses had been built. Looking out from the front of the station, a deep lake with shimmering white waves reflected the beautiful sunlight. The reeds along the shore of the lake were long, swaying gently in the wind. As soon as I saw this scene, I remembered when I was a naive and lively child, often barefoot, catching fish and shrimp in the shallow waters of the lake, sometimes hiding in the reeds to play. That was the past, and now it's just something to long for. Therefore, when some children who didn't know me tilted their heads to look at me, I couldn't help but curse myself, "Ah! I've wandered for so many days, and what have I gained to offer my hometown?" Shameful, ah! Just a body full of terrible wounds!

Leaving the train station and dragging my feet back to my village, I saw the branches and leaves of the village's bamboo grove swaying, emitting a rustling sound, seeming to sigh, or perhaps mock me. However, I finally bravely stepped over the threshold of my old home.

The house was as silent as death. The ground seemed to be covered with green moss, and a cold air emanated from the dark house, causing the wandering son to feel sorrow: "Where is the home from my childhood? It's too desolate here!" Indeed, I remember very clearly that when I was a child, my brothers and I were always laughing and jumping around, seemingly unaware of sorrow. Now, the pitiful old home has been immersed in a circle without sunlight.

The frail old mother ran out. The sudden return of her son filled her with surprise, and tears of joy welled up in her eyes:

"Ah! You've come back! I've been dreaming of your return!"

Yes, she had always been waiting for her son's return in her dreams. When her unusual face stirred my heart, I could only say a sighing sentence that couldn't comfort her wounds:

"Yes! Mother, I have returned safely!"

Mr. San 222

— Er Lang

Although Mr. San seemed to be a foreign academician in the eyes of the villagers, he had never held an official position outside. He had only worked in academic professions such as university provost and university professor. This time, when he returned home for the summer vacation, the villagers treated it as a major event of "returning home in glory," congratulating him and giving gifts for several days. They simply regarded him as even more important than the township head, and some even publicly declared, "Now that Mr. San has returned in glory, we should elect him as the township head so that we can all have prestige."

One day, when the township head went to the city, a case of robbery and attempted murder occurred in the village. Everyone escorted the bandit and the victim to Mr. San's house, saying, "Mr. San's word is final. You can decide how to handle it. There's no need to wait for the township head to return." The villagers respected and admired him that much. However, after questioning about the case, the victim was unwilling to be the plaintiff and only begged for a quick resolution. This made Mr. San hesitate. The case occurred as follows: —

The owner of the small cigarette shop at the village entrance bought twenty or so packs of cigarettes from the city and asked Lao Da, who pushed a cart, to bring them home as a favor. Unexpectedly, on the way, Lao Da was knocked unconscious by a man with a stick, who stole the cigarettes and ran away. After he woke up, he shouted "Robber!" as he chased after him. Villagers gathered from the fields and caught the man. They had already beaten him, which would have been enough to release him, but someone said, "We have always been peaceful here. We have never had a case of robbery and attempted murder like this. That's unacceptable!" So they brought him to Mr. San's house.

"Escort him to the county," Mr. San said. However, the cigarette shop owner pleaded, "Don't escort him to the county, Mr. San. I beg you to do me a favor." Mr. San was surprised and widened his eyes. "Why don't you want to escort him to the county?" The owner said, "You know, twenty or so packs of cigarettes are only worth twenty or so dollars. Even if they were stolen, it would be nothing. Even treating the injured Lao Da, who pushes the cart, wouldn't cost much. If we escort him to the county, you know, I'd have to close my shop and accompany him to the county for the trial, ask a scribe to write the indictment, and curry favor with everyone in the county. Twenty or so dollars wouldn't even cover the expenses."

Mr. San lowered his eyelids, thinking. "There's some truth to that. But if we don't escort him to the county, what should we do?" He walked a circle in the room, the eyes of the crowd following his footsteps, silently. Suddenly, Mr. San stopped and said, "If we don't escort him to the county, let's escort him to the district office." The owner was still adamant, "Mr. San, please do me a favor and just beat him and let him go. If we escort him to the district office, I would still have to accompany him for a trip, and no one would take care of my shop's business." Mr. San ignored him, and with a wave of his hand, the villagers pulled the man away. The owner sighed, knowing that trouble was inevitable, and didn't dare to grumble anymore, following the villagers out of Mr. San's house.

The man knelt on the ground in Mr. San's house, crying and weeping, tears and snot flowing together. Mr. San had also been moved by his compassion. However, the case was too serious, "robbery and attempted murder," how could Mr. San dare to release him?

However, the next day, it was said that the man had run away in the night. The district office had a militia, how could he have escaped? The person reporting said, "The cigarette shop owner used money to have the militia release him." Mr. San nodded and smiled. The responsibility was now the district office's, nothing to do with him. The reason why he, Mr. San, didn't dare to release him yesterday was because of the issue of responsibility. Now it was good, he had no responsibility. When the township head returned, he would have an explanation. He smiled and said, "That man is also quite pitiful." Therefore, he thought that if there hadn't been that stick, he wouldn't have committed a crime.

However, another question lingered in Mr. San's mind: The villagers were afraid of going to the county government, which showed that the corrupt judicial practices of the county government had not been eliminated.

Under the Banyan Tree 223

— Shen Wu

The south wind brought the summer season. Half-red and half-white lotus flowers bloomed in the lotus pond, with green leaves interspersed between the red and white flowers, making the pond even more vibrant.

The cicadas chirped loudly in the treetops; looking up, the lush greenery completely blocked the sun, occasionally a few faint rays of sunlight sneaking through the gaps, turning into scattered spots of light under a large patch of shade. The scent of lush green leaves drifted in the breeze, and lingering under the shade of this tree to admire the scenery of the lotus pond made it especially easy to feel as leisurely as recalling ancient times or reminiscing about the past. At least, here, I felt separated from the chaotic and turbulent real world by many centuries. If I were a famous scholar flipping through ancient books or some kind of poet or lyricist, this would be a great place to chant or admire. Unfortunately, I am just an ordinary person, and under the tight coercion of the whip of life, this can only be my only place of rest.

I have no home. I am rushing on a road that will never end, ever since the year I fell from my mother's womb until now. — Perhaps just like a lost fledgling, flying around with a large flock of birds. But I don't know where my home is. Vaguely, I found a broken plank in the sea, no, I found a deserted island; so I stayed on this deserted island, lingering under this banyan tree for this time…

During the day, I wrapped two rough loaves of bread in half a piece of old newspaper and walked to the edge of this pond. As soon as I reached the shade of the banyan tree, my steps suddenly stopped, and without needing to choose, I sat down on the grass and stuffed the bread into my mouth like a hungry tiger. Sometimes, I would also wade into the pond to pick one or two lotus flowers, peel off the petals and scatter them on the ground, then spread the tender yellow stamens on the grass to dry them and take them home to use as tea.

Night after night, the stars in the sky shone with burning eyes. I wandered alone under the shade of the tree, listening to the croaking of frogs late at night. The green fields fell into a boundless darkness, and my tiny eyes could not see the vast horizon. Occasionally, I saw a few specks of light and heard some sounds of wind blowing through the grass, as well as slow and steady footsteps. There were still people catching frogs in the fields day and night, so in my own desolate heart, I also found some comfort.

I have no sorrow. Forever embracing a lonely heart, following a group of older and more elderly people, drifting from here to there, now I have drifted to this deserted island. But where is that group? They have already fallen, one by one, like autumn leaves, in the midst of dangerous wind and rain. From then on, only I was left alone.

I lingered under the banyan tree, recalling the past. I felt that I could no longer be alone. When I heard those distant footsteps, I stubbornly struggled up from the ground again. Looking at the branches and trunk of the banyan tree, I felt that it was not yet old, and I myself was still young. The summer wind could not blow away the leaves of youth, I could still struggle and continue my future — weren't there still a group of young people like me ahead? …

The Naked Feet Problem in "Peach Blossom Dream" 231

Theaters and cinemas, in order to rectify the audience, do not allow those from the lower class society who are barefoot and not wearing socks to enter the seats. However, modern women who expose their jade toes and wear hollow-out leather shoes can enter and leave gracefully, and the waiters serve them for fear of being inadequate. This is indeed an incomprehensible strange problem. In the "Peach Blossom Dream" directed by Mr. Du Yu of the Shanghai Film Company, the above situation is adopted in the performance, which is funny and abrupt, and has never been seen before, and the seriousness of the poor and rich classes is implicitly contained in it. Mr. Du Yu's intelligence can be seen here.

The Shenbao Local Supplement, Automobile Weekly

Experiment on the Number of Times Brakes are Used 233

— Yu

How many times on average does a driver on the road need to stop the car to avoid pedestrians or due to traffic obstructions? This is a very interesting question. From a driving perspective, it reveals how often the brakes are used by the average person. Now, the question has been answered through practical experimentation: an average driver on a busy street stops the car approximately once every minute. In other words, brakes are used about every sixty seconds.

The above-mentioned frequency of brake usage is not based on mere calculation but on actual field experiments. This experiment was conducted by the Automobile Club of Michigan in the United States. In order to find a qualified "typical" driver, they carefully selected participants who were neither complete beginners nor experienced professionals. Both categories were considered unsuitable; beginners lack the necessary skills, and professionals are too advanced. Therefore, they chose a woman named Eve F. Lindsey for this testing. The Plymouth Motor Corporation supported this endeavor, and the results were highly satisfactory.

Ms. Lindsey drove a new Plymouth sedan. The entire journey lasted eight hours. During these eight hours, Ms. Lindsey used the brakes a total of 547 times. To ensure accuracy and proper recording, a connected "stop counter" was installed next to the brake pedal. Thus, every time the brakes were applied, the counter faithfully recorded it.

The experiment took place in Detroit, the well-known automotive manufacturing center of the United States, under the supervision of officials from the Michigan Automobile Club. To ensure impartiality, two notaries public were present at the start and end to inspect everything. The start was overseen by John Flaherty of the local police traffic committee, and Captain Wesley Brown of the Public Safety Bureau was responsible for verifying the stop counter records at the finish line. Ms. Lindsey drove on various roads in different areas. Some parts of the city were bustling, while others were quiet. In busy areas, the population was dense, and traffic was naturally heavy. In quiet areas, the population was sparse, and the traffic situation was different. Moreover, the time of day also had a significant impact. In the morning, suburban residents were busy going to the city and business centers, causing heavy traffic in the urban areas. Conversely, in the late afternoon, people returned to the suburbs, creating a traffic jam on the connecting roads, resembling a long, endless belt. Ms. Lindsey drove in these diverse environments, using the brakes only when absolutely necessary, based on the surrounding conditions. Therefore, she did not overuse the brakes during the entire journey.

The frequency of Ms. Lindsey's brake usage varied depending on the time of day and traffic conditions. During the first hour and a half of her driving, she used the brakes a total of 100 times, meaning she stopped 100 times. Between 11:00 AM and 1:00 PM, she stopped 34 times, but from 12:00 PM to 1:00 PM, she stopped 88 times. This is likely due to the lunch hour in urban areas, when many people are on the road. Especially in areas with concentrated offices, employees rush into the streets as soon as the clock strikes twelve, increasing the number of pedestrians. When cars encounter pedestrians crossing the road, they naturally have to brake to avoid them, thus increasing the frequency of brake usage.

The experiment lasted eight hours. During this time, Ms. Lindsey traveled a total distance of 143.3 miles, with an average speed of slightly over 18 miles per hour. This speed was considered moderate, not particularly high, mainly because the areas she traversed did not allow for faster driving. There were also continuous streams of vehicles and pedestrians. Ms. Lindsey's maximum speed during the entire journey was only 30 miles per hour, and most of the time, her speed was around 25 miles per hour.

After the experiment, Mr. Halsted stated that the results showed that reliable and effective brakes are essential for driving in urban areas and cannot be ignored. Ms. Lindsey used the brakes nearly once a minute, or three times per mile. Therefore, Mr. Halsted concluded that he was very impressed with these numbers, and other drivers should deeply understand the importance of brakes in driving.

Important Notes on Tire Usage 234

— Chen Xing

Tire Pressure: Always keep tire pressure within the specified limits. The normal tire pressure limit is the minimum. It is never appropriate to reduce tire pressure slightly, but it should exceed it slightly. For example, if the specified tire pressure is 32 pounds, the pressure should be inflated to 34 pounds. Check tire pressure weekly. If it is found to be slightly reduced, it must be replenished. A good tire will not leak more than two pounds of air per week. If it reaches this number, it is necessary to pay close attention to the tire, especially the valve. An old inner tube is, of course, more likely to leak than a new one. If your inner tube is too old and leaks quickly, it is better to replace it with a new inner tube to avoid excessive wear and tear on the outer tire due to insufficient air pressure. Excessive air pressure will cause unexpected wear and tear on the center of the tire, and insufficient air pressure will cause undue damage to both sides of the tire.

Whenever you remove and reinstall a tire, or install a new tire, do not start driving long distances until you are sure that the air pressure is appropriate. The reason is that when a tire is mounted on a steel rim and begins to run, it is subjected to extremely strong pressure, which will leak several pounds of air and damage your tire due to insufficient air pressure. Therefore, the best way is to inflate the tire fully after it is mounted, drive four or five miles, stop the car, and check it. If it is found to be insufficient, it must be replenished immediately. New tires leak more quickly in the first few weeks of use and should also be noted.

Do not always use tires on the same wheels. By constantly moving your tires from one wheel to another, the wear and tear on the tires can be greatly reduced. Your spare tire must also be included in the rotation process and should not be left unused for more than six months, as it will wear out very quickly over time. Therefore, a more economical way to use tires is to rotate them on all wheels of the car. After many car experiences, engineers have established a cyclical rotation method to facilitate implementation. Every time the car travels 5,000 miles (8,000 kilometers), the tires can be rotated clockwise, that is, move the right front tire to the right rear wheel, the right rear tire to the spare wheel, and the spare wheel to the left rear wheel, and so on. If there are two spare tires, both must be included in the rotation. Another valuable task is often overlooked, and you must also pay attention to it. If one side of the steel rim of the wheel is always facing the outside of the car, the tire should be rotated on the same wheel from time to time. The side facing outward can be changed to face inward. A tire that is often used on the same wheel will inevitably cause uneven wear and tear. For example, the degree of wear of the front and rear tires must be different. The tires on the left side are more prone to damage because they are more accessible to the roadside, and the tire walls may be scratched by the street edges.

It is generally believed that the danger of a rear tire bursting is less than that of a front tire bursting, so old tires are installed on the rear wheels. This view should not be relied upon. That is not right. Many trials have proven that the danger caused by a burst tire on the rear wheel is not less than the front tire. When the road surface is slippery, if the rear tire bursts, the tire will immediately go flat, and the anti-skid tread will lose its effect. The rear end of the car is the part that receives power to propel the vehicle forward, which will increase the skidding of the vehicle to a surprising degree. The danger at this time is indeed greater than the burst of the front tire. For this reason, tires that are in relatively good condition but without tread should be avoided as much as possible on the rear wheels.

Unless driving fire trucks, ambulances and police vehicles, do not turn at high speeds, as this damages tires more than anything else. When you turn the steering wheel at high speed, the tires will naturally turn with it, but the tires are still moving forward due to inertia. In this way, the tire wall is subjected to a terrible squeeze, and the entire tire will slide over to one side of the road by an inch or more. If you want to know how much damage this causes to the tire, you can take a new tire, make a mark, and press it with all your strength to make it roll forward and backward on a new concrete road six inches wide about 500 times, and then check it. The degree of wear and tear is often less than that of a new tire mounted on a car turning at 50 miles per hour.

Except to avoid causing an accident, do not use the brakes violently. Violent use of the brakes will damage the brake bands, brake drums, and other parts of the vehicle, not to mention, but it can have terrible results on the tires. When you have braked the wheels to a stop, inertia still forces the car to move forward. Therefore, if the braking action is very sudden, the car will slide forward, and it may wipe off a large piece of rubber from your four tires. In addition, violent use of the brakes will cause severe vibrations to the bottom edge of the tire, causing damage to the rubber weaving layer and the junction between the two. Therefore, the brakes must be used very gently so as not to cause unexpected damage to the tires. The braking force applied to the four wheels should be evenly consistent, otherwise some tires will be subjected to the same wear and tear mentioned above. Therefore, a good brake calibration device must be carried with you at all times so that it can be used to calibrate the brakes so that they are evenly consistent.

Your wheels must be inspected and calibrated regularly, both front and rear wheels. To ensure accurate calibration, it can be performed by specialized personnel. Whether there is anything wrong with the front wheels must be checked with a certain device. Any speculation will not be accurate. If your car is old, and the inspection reveals that some parts have worn out, causing the vehicle to sway, you must repair it, or even replace the new bearing, steering pin and bushing. A swaying wheel will leap off the ground, which is extremely damaging to the tire. If you cannot calibrate the wheels correctly and cannot correct the swaying of the wheels, you will not only greatly increase the cost of tire repair, but also frequently change new tires. In addition, the swaying tire causes irregular friction between the tire and the road surface, so no matter how strong the tire is, it will inevitably suffer unexpected wear and tear.

Inspect your tires from time to time for anything stuck in them. If stone chips are embedded in the tread pattern of the tire, they must be removed. If they are left in, they will pierce the tread and weaving layer, causing the weaving layer to be damaged and broken. This will cause the tire to burst and vulcanize. The safest way is to use a swirl chisel from time to time to remove the stone chips stuck in the tire. If there are small nails and other sharp objects, they should be removed one by one.

If the speed is too high, the tire will generate high heat. If the tire is overheated due to the climate, the wear and tear will exceed the normal level. When the climate is cool and the road is wet, the heat of the tire can be dissipated, and the wear and tear can be reduced. Therefore, the degree of tire wear and tear in winter and during the two seasons is less than in summer. In extremely hot weather, driving on dry roads, coupled with extremely high speeds, the tires generate high heat and increase the speed of wear and tear. If the tires have already been damaged a lot, this situation can cause the tires to burst and other similar serious incidents.

Starting too abruptly causes the same damage to the tire as a sudden stop, but in the opposite direction. Starting too abruptly causes the wheels to slip and roll, and the tires are greatly damaged as a result. Therefore, under certain circumstances, you can start in second gear to prevent the wheels from slipping and damaging the tires.

Do not let the tires hit or run over the curbs. Such abuse will cause the tires to be injured. Your inner tube will be clamped by the steel rim, and the weaving layer will break due to loosening. After a few days or a month, your tire will burst as a result. If you still cannot find the real reason for the burst at this time, you will blame others unreasonably.

When you are driving, if you suddenly feel that the steering is different, you must slowly stop the car and carefully check each tire according to law. This is often caused by the tire about to burst. In this way, you can not only find the defects of the tire, repair and replace it, and avoid danger, but also, the tire will not burst, and you can save a lot of repair costs.

Automotive News from Abroad 235

— Yu

Unifying the Period for Car Tax Certificates: Thomas Henry, president of the American Automobile Association, noting that thousands of cars are detained each year for expired tax certificates in various states, proposed that the period for car tax certificates should be unified across all states to avoid many troubles for drivers and all management disputes. According to Mr. Henry, the period for car tax certificates varies greatly among the states, and there are already many disputes. The confusion in the future will be even more significant. If the country can stipulate a uniform period for tax certificates, the benefits will certainly be many. In the forty states and the District of Columbia in the United States, the period for car registration and tax certificates begins on January 1st, and the end and grace dates vary. Alabama starts taxing from October 1st, South Carolina on November 1st, South Dakota on April 1st, Vermont on April 1st, Virginia on April 1st, Utah on March 1st, and West Virginia on July 1st. Mr. Henry also said that five states are currently proposing changes: Delaware, Pennsylvania, and Wisconsin from January 1st to July 1st, Minnesota to April 14th, and Texas to July 1st. Henry finally hoped that the American Automobile Association would be able to rescue thousands of detained car drivers.
